NOSAS camp to go to hell without being warned of the damning deficiency
of their NOSAS faith.
        Alternatively, if we who believe OSAS-N are right, then the only
loving thing we can to do is warn those sitting in their houses of conditional
security that their houses have a faulty foundation built upon a concrete
mixture of Jesus and works—an amalgamation that leads to damnation.
Otherwise, their blood will be on our hands. Contrastively, if we are wrong,
then we are guilty only of insisting that those holding NOSAS need to adopt
the truth of OSAS—a truth that our critics within OSAS-U would concede to
be correct anyway. Basically, no harm, no foul, if OSAS-N is correct.
        In summary, securitists are taking an awful risk with the salvation of
others if securitists assume that a failure to believe in OSAS does not
jeopardize the saving potential of faith. If one is to err on the side of caution,
then one must side with the necessity of security. Granted, it is better not to
err. But let those securitists who think that belief in security is unnecessary
be absolutely certain that they are right. Otherwise, let them not throw
caution to the wind. The best policy is to insist on the necessity of security.

Necessity of Security
       As noted at the GES Webboard and by the opposing article posted
therein, many passages condition eternal life on performance. The
contention by the OSAS-U constituency was that the confusion caused by
the biblical diffusion of eternal life as a gift in some passages versus a
reward in other passages presents a nullification of OSAS-N. Supposedly,
securitists cannot insist upon the necessity of unconditional security
(specifically regarding eternal life) because Scripture frequently speaks of
conditional security (pertaining to eternal life).

       Confusion is no Excuse
       As noted and charted herein, Scripture speaks of eternal life as a gift,
yet on multiple occasions Scripture describes eternal life as a reward.
Arguably, in some passages it is hard to discern which aspect of eternal life
the biblical speaker has in mind. Even so, does the existence of gray prove
that black and white do not exist? Not at all.
       We are not free to interchange the conditions for a gift and a reward
and think that we get the same result. For example, the requirement for
eternal life in Jn 12:25-26 is that one serve Jesus. The aspect of eternal life
that one gains by serving Jesus is associated with saving one’s soul in terms
of being honored by God. Securitists have no trouble recognizing that this
passage is talking about obtaining eternal life as a reward. Are securitists
Appendix 1. Broken Allegiances                                         Page 95

then free to port this condition to Jn 3:16 and pretend that they get the same
result? Hardly! Such a monstrous importation is an imposter of the gospel:

 •   For God so loved the world, that He gave His only begotten Son, that
     whoever serves Him should not perish, but have eternal life. (Jn 3:16)

        According to the logical implications of the OSAS-U theory, legalists
who believe that they get the free gift of eternal life by serving Jesus with
their earthly lives will be given eternal life. Perish the thought!
        Lest it be thought that this concern is merely theoretically, I will
insert an example that occurred today (the day I added this appendix). My
family and I were attending the Easter service at our church. One would
hope that on Easter, of all days, a pastor would get the gospel right and stress
that Jesus did everything (performance wise) that was necessary to provide
for redemption. Our pastor started off well by noting from Mt 26:57ff that
Jesus was put on trial by the religious authorities, by people who boasted of
their love for God and of their service to God. True enough, those religious
people who were seeking to crucify Jesus thought that they were better than
everyone else (including Jesus) because of their devotion to God. If today’s
legalists were logically consistent, then they would have to admit that they
think that they are better than everyone else (and that they know better than
Jesus how to motive godly living).
        Our pastor eventually proceeded to invite people in the congregation
to love and serve Jesus so that they could go to heaven. Our pastor proved to
be a gospel imposter when he made serving Jesus equivalent to believing in
Jesus. Subsequently, in the course of this same sermon, he denied that the
salvation he was offering was contingent upon performance. Clearly, he was
speaking irrationally. Service is a performance concept.
                     Illustration 46. Believe Equals Serve
Page 96                                     Woolly Wolves and Woolless Sheep


       Such pastors are prudent enough not to make such statements back to
back so that the insanity of their posturing will not be immediately obvious.
Thus, one suspects that they realize that their theology is suspect. Despite
their pastoral claims counter wise, they manifestly do not believe that one is
saved by simply believing in Jesus. (Moreover, our pastor berated those who
thought they could be saved freely by believing in Jesus for fire insurance
without serving Jesus.) By specifying that belief is the requirement for
salvation and then by stating that service is required for this same salvation,
our pastor had redefined belief as service with this association. Then he tried
to disassociate this service with performance—a double error.21
       Is the OSAS-U advocate free to tell those pastors who confuse service
with belief that doing so is okay? Never! OSAS-U advocates know that it is
wrong to confuse the condition of service laid out in Jn 12:25-26 with the
condition of belief that is spelled out in Jn 3:16. My fellow securitists in the
opposing OSAS-U camp have no right to consider any pastor a believer
when that pastor has redefined saving faith as service!
       Similarly, in Jn 4:36, gathering fruit evangelistically for the
enjoyment or procurement of eternal life (zoe) is associated with receiving
(lambano) wages (i.e., misthos). In this context, the eternal life being reaped
as a wage by the evangelistic labors is a reward for evangelistic activity.
This same biblical writer also gives this evangelistic invitation: “Let the one
who wishes take (lambano) the water of life (zoe) without cost”
(Rev 22:17). Is one justified in transposing the descriptions between the two
texts so as to make the latter text read: “Let the one who wishes take
(lambano) the water of life (zoe) as a wage”? Absolutely not! Securitists are
not free to say that those who mistake the water of life as a wage are saved.
       Securitists cannot allow the transposition of the conditions and
descriptions (in the name of confusion), and then pretend that those doing so
get the desired result. For one thing, the context forbids it. For a second
thing, Scripture is replete with texts warning that salvation from eternal
damnation must be received as a free gift apart from works. Those goats and
wolves that stand before God in judgment will not be able to excuse
themselves by appealing to confusion. Goats are not free, contrary to OSAS-
U claims otherwise, to twist the words of Scripture to suit their conditional
security and think that they will get unconditional security as the result. For
another thing, much of the confusion is a result of judgment.
       In the beginning of the OT, God confused the language of the whole
earth at the tower of Babel as an expression of judgment on their
disobedience and to confound their I-can-work-my-way-to-heaven attitude
(Gen 11:4-9). In the beginning of the NT, rather than confuse their language,
since God had already done that previously, the Lord confused the people
who were trying to work their way to heaven by speaking to them in
confounding language—parables and other figurative means of speech.
Appendix 1. Broken Allegiances                                       Page 97


      11
        And He was saying to them, “To you has been given the
      mystery of the kingdom of God; but those who are outside get
      everything in parables, 12 in order that while seeing, they may
      see and not perceive; and while hearing, they may hear and not

       In the OT, God confused the language of those people trying to get to
heaven by means of their works in order to confound them. In the NT, He
simply spoke to them in confounding language. Whether you are a poor
hourly worker or a rich young ruler trying to work your way to heaven, do
not be surprised if the Lord allows you to stew in confusion—such is the
Lord’s judgment on those trying to work their way to heaven.
       Securitists have no right to offer assurance to those babbling in
legalism. The Bible was written in a time of war and encoded from those
trying to work their way to heaven—whether they do so by bricks or by
good works. Moreover, even when Jesus was talking with His followers, He
used hard to understand figures, even though it hindered their understanding
and offended some of His followers, even to the point that some of His
believing followers left Him (Jn 6:65-66; 13:7; 16:25). The Lord did not
always go out of His way to make it easy for others to understand Him.
Sometimes He expected His listeners to strive to understand what He was
saying (cp. Lk 13:24). Nevertheless, Jesus held them accountable. Securitists
are playing with fire when they say that the Lord will not hold those
accountable who misunderstand Him just because some of what He has said
has the potential to confuse them. If Jesus did not excuse the confused, can
we?
Page 98                                      Woolly Wolves and Woolless Sheep

       The Narrow Gate is Narrow
       The passage regarding the narrow gate is a favorite text among
proveitists and securitists alike: “Enter by the narrow gate; for the gate is
wide, and the way is broad that leads to destruction, and many are those who
enter by it. For the gate is small, and the way is narrow that leads to life, and
few are those who find it” (Mt 7:13-14).
                    Illustration 47. Broad Gate of NOSAS




       Performatists are inclined to see the narrow gate as the believer’s
performance. Therefore, they trust in Christ plus performance for their
oxymoronic costly-free gift of eternal life. According to proveitists,
performance proves whether or not you were ever saved in the beginning.
Additionally, performance ultimately determines if you will be saved at the
ending. Therefore, proveitists seek to narrow the gate to heaven by only
allowing those who live up to their performance requirements to enter.
Numerically, however, this results in a broad gate because from early times
the majority within professing Christendom has believed wrongly that
profession must be sufficiently matched with performance to result in
entrance.
                   Illustration 48. Narrow Gate of OSAS-N




       Securitists, by demarcation, are inclined to see the narrow gate as
saving faith: saving faith being understood as faith alone in Christ alone for
the free gift of eternal life which is given in response to such faith. Saving
Appendix 1. Broken Allegiances                                           Page 99

faith determines whether or not one is saved from hell. The narrow gate is
faith in the narrow path, and the narrow path is Christ alone. Therefore,
entrance into the possession of eternal life as a free gift, and, ultimately, into
heaven itself, is conditioned on faith alone in Christ alone. Numerically as
well as biblically, this is a much smaller number of professing Christendom.
                   Illustration 49. Broader Gate of OSAS-U




       Those securitists who simply perceive the narrow gate as being
saving faith in Christ put themselves in quite a dilemma when they jettison
the restricting aspect of that faith so as to include those proveitists who
believe that their performance has a role to play in their being allowed into
heaven. By making OSAS unnecessary, OSAS-U opens the flood gates for
those who think that works are necessary. With their all-inclusive theology,
OSAS-U advocates logically would flood heaven with practically (if not
actually) every Christian legalist who has ever existed.*
         Illustration 50. Three Contending Views of the Narrow Gate




*
 Of the three options, the narrow gate of OSAS-U is the broadest gate.
OSAS-U opens its gate to both NOSAS and OSAS-N. Mathematically,
OSAS-U = NOSAS + OSAS-N.
Page 100                                     Woolly Wolves and Woolless Sheep


       Whereas in this Matthean context, Jesus excludes the majority of His
followers from entering heaven, OSAS-U practically opens the gate to all of
Jesus’ followers, regardless of their legalistic inclinations. The OSAS-U
results tend to get wild. If you believe that you have to be baptized in order
to go to heaven, then come on down to the front of the isle: the price is right.
You simply have to pay the necessary dues to make it to heaven. If you
believe that you have to endure to the end to be saved from hell, then come
on down to the front of the isle; such a perception will work too. Any and
every Christian legalist is offered entrance as long as he or she has trusted, to
some extent, in the resurrected Christ for eternal life. The narrow gate is
turned into a broad gate by OSAS-U securitists.22
       Jesus, in stark contrast, excludes those who trust in Him plus their
performance for kingdom entrance (Mt 7:22). He excludes them on the very
basis of their performance (Mt 7:23). They point to the works they did in His
name. Certainly, those appealing to their works done in the Lord’s name as a
collaborating reason that the Lord should let them into heaven are in some
manner trusting in the Lord for entrance into heaven. Surely, the vast
majority of those rejected by the Lord on that day will have believed that
Jesus died on the cross for their sins, that He rose from the dead, and that He
was God in the flesh. Yet, as evidenced in their Matthean confusion, those
rejected by the Lord trusted in their God-enabled works as necessary proof
that they were saved—as proof that they belonged to God. The prevailing
consensus among NOSAS and OSAS proponents alike would be that these
followers of Christ had believed in the Lord for salvific benefits, but their
faith was soterically defective.
       OSAS-U, on the other hand, cannot find the faith of these professing
Christians defective soterically on the basis of their performance since
OSAS-U does not condition the salvific sufficiency of faith on its
performance. In other words, as a branch of OSAS, OSAS-U cannot use the
NOSAS filter of performance to narrow the gate. Conversely, OSAS-U
cannot use the OSAS-N filter of faith in Christ alone to narrow the gate. The
proponents of OSAS-U are left with nothing by which to narrow the gate.
       Strangely, when I confronted these OSAS-U proponents with the fact
that they were opening the gates of heaven to practically every Christian
legalist under the sun, leaving them with no means by which to narrow the
gate, the responses I received were that (1) the narrow gate is not a gate to
heaven or that (2) these people in Mt 7:22 did not believe in Jesus (at all) for
eternal life!
       Both of these OSAS-U reactions would be rejected by the
overwhelming majority throughout church history. The OSAS-U proponents
were basing their argument that believing in OSAS is unnecessary on the
fact that the majority of professing Christendom throughout church history
has believed in NOSAS. At the same time, these OSAS-U advocates were
Appendix 1. Broken Allegiances                                      Page 101

trying to discredit the majority opinion when it came to acknowledging that
those rejected by the narrow gate were in some manner trusting in Christ for
their entrance into heaven. Astounding! That is a mighty long limb upon
which to climb out. Those in OSAS-U who reject the narrow gate as leading
to heaven must climb out on a very narrow limb indeed.23
       If those in NOSAS are allowed into heaven, then who within
professing Christendom is excluded by the narrow gate? In contrast to
OSAS-U, advocates of OSAS-N have no trouble answering this question.
Those professing believers who try to work their way into heaven are
excluded by the narrow gate. Hence, the NOSAS group is excluded.
Historically, the majority throughout church history has believed in NOSAS.
Therefore, those who believe in conditional security fit the profile of those
excluded from entrance.

      Legalism is Not a Saving Gospel
        Both the Apostle Paul and Martin Luther rejected legalism as a
potential means of salvation. The irony of ironies is that even many legalists
acknowledge that legalism is a deadly perversion of the gospel. As
embarrassing as it is to admit, such legalists show better sense than those of
my fellow securitists who open up the floodgates for legalists. While various
brands of legalism are anathemizing one another, OSAS-U opens the doors
of heaven to all of them!
        Proponents of the so-called new perspectives in Pauline studies have
concluded that Paul and Luther were all wet when it came to thinking that
Judaism was saturated with legalism. However, as some critics of this new
perspective rightly have pointed out, Paul’s criticisms were not limited to
strict legalism. God-enabled legalism is legalism too!
        Jesus Himself confronts and denounces God-enabled legalism. In
Jesus’ parable of the Pharisee and the publican, the Pharisee opens his prayer
with thanks to God for his performance. His legalistic prayer could be
summarized as: God, thank You that I don’t live like that publican. The
Pharisee attributes his righteous performance to God’s enabling grace with
his, “Thank You.” And Jesus sentences this God-thanking Pharisee to hell.
Why? Because the Pharisee is trusting in his God-enabled performance as a
means for justification from eternal damnation (Lk 18:9-14). Jesus equates
trusting in God-enabled performance for such justification with trusting in
one’s self that one is righteous. These God-thanking Pharisees searched the
Scriptures diligently and scrupulously trying to keep the scriptural
commands in order to obtain eternal life (Jn 5:39). If confusion were an
alibi, then Jesus would not have pronounced a damning sentence upon them.
Confusion does not provide exculpation for self-justification.
        From Jesus’ statement in Luke, we see that they trusted in God and in
themselves for their righteousness and that Jesus denounced this as self-
Page 102                                   Woolly Wolves and Woolless Sheep
righteousness. From Jesus’ rebuke in John, we also observe that they trusted
in Scripture that they were righteous. The problem was that they trusted in
their observance of Scriptural commands related to performance for eternal
life as a means to enter the kingdom (Mt 19:20). Their modern day
counterparts still trust in God and in themselves for righteousness via
trusting in their observance of scriptural commands related to performance,
such as taking up their cross daily (Lk 9:23).
           Illustration 51. God-Enabled Performance for Heaven




      Attack From Within
        Neolegalism asserts that what Jesus did for us on the cross is
insufficient to accomplish our salvation. According to them, we must take up
our cross and follow in ongoing obedience to His commands to make it to
heaven. Neolegalists, in effect, spit on the cross of Christ by saying that
what Jesus did on the cross was insufficient to pay for our eternal
redemption. They further claim that the past grace shown on the cross must
be supplemented with future grace in terms of God-enabled performance in
order for recipients of God’s grace to make it to heaven. Like all legalists,
they think that their God-enabled performance must somehow* be added to
the finished work of Christ in order for them to make it to heaven.


*
  Making God-enabled performance necessary proof is a favorite ploy used by
such legalists in adding works to faith as a secondary (yet equally necessary)
condition for salvation from hell.
Appendix 1. Broken Allegiances                                       Page 103

                Illustration 52. Is it finished? Does it matter?




        OSAS-U advocates do not believe that God will be so narrow as to
only accept narrow belief—a belief that is narrowed to trusting in Christ for
OSAS. OSAS-U opens the gates of heaven to Neolegalism.
        As an advocate of OSAS-N, I do not believe that neolegalistic belief
is saving. Contrary to the claims of Neolegalists, what Jesus did on the cross
was enough to procure our salvation. Furthermore, even if one were to adopt
the perspective that Jesus currently is exercising soteric advocacy in heaven
for us, it would simply be more than enough.24
        OSAS-U, on the other hand, looks on the debate, in terms of what
composes saving faith, and says that it does not matter if legalists claim that
what Jesus did on the cross is not enough. As an advocate of OSAS-N, I am
opposed to such an OSAS-U attitude.
        Admittedly, OSAS-U is not legalism. Thus, I have not pictured it as a
sheep in wolf’s skin. Nevertheless, it has fangs like a wolf. OSAS-U acts
like legalism in attacking the necessity of unconditional security. Those
within OSAS-U have pledged an allegiance to OSAS, yet under some
sympathy to NOSAS, they have subsequently denied the subjective
necessity of security. This alliance is disastrous. Instead of attacking the
gospel from without, OSAS-U attacks it from within. Rather than
confronting legalism as being a deadly distortion of the gospel, the OSAS-U
alliance with NOSAS coddles legalistic notions.
Page 104   Woolly Wolves and Woolless Sheep
                             Appendix 2.
              Oscillation is not Salvation
        A typical argument advanced by OSAS-U supposes that in a moment
of oscillation between believing two contradictory statements, legalists will
come to saving faith. According to this highly optimistic projection, most
misguided legalists will make it into heaven. For example, suppose that on a
given Sunday a congregation is being told, as is frequently the case, that
eternal life is a free gift that costs them (implicitly) everything, and their
legalistic pastor withholds the mention of the costly price tag until the
invitation.

Theoretical Salvation
        During the course of the sermon, while the freeness of the gift is
being stressed, could an individual sitting in the pew respond in saving faith
to the correct emphasis being placed on the freeness of the gift before the
invitation is given, at which time the price tag of performance is added?
Yes—at least theoretically.
                 Illustration 53. The Swing of the Pendulum
Page 106                                     Woolly Wolves and Woolless Sheep


       I have no problem admitting that those hearing a pseudo Lordship
Salvationist speaking out of both sides of his mouth might actually respond
savingly, through the conviction of the Holy Spirit, while he is speaking
correctly out of the right side of his mouth in stressing that one is saved from
hell by believing in Jesus. On the other hand, I believe a saving response in
such a context happens infrequently. For congregants will probably not
respond savingly before their pastor speaks wrongly out of the other side of
his mouth and equates believing in Jesus with serving Jesus.
       One major problem with the rosy-colored OSAS-U vision that
projects a high number of such misguided people actually responding
savingly to the correct part of the sermon is that congregants will have sit
under a countless number of such inconsistent sermons. Unknowingly, they
will have made an unshakable mental association between the price tag of
human performance and what was supposed to be the free gift of eternal life.
Without realizing it, they will have been conditioned to assume that the free
gift costs them something, if not everything.
       Obviously, such a costly-free proposition is illogical. But the human
mind does not necessarily function logically. Two contradictory propositions
can be believed simultaneously. Therefore, in this theology of inconsistency,
OSAS-U argues that people in such a state of confusion are saved either
because (in the OSAS-U opinion): (1) legalists do not have to believe in
OSAS, or (2) in a positive moment of oscillation legalistic congregations do
believe in OSAS, although not to the exclusion of NOSAS, or (3) during the
forward, positive swing of the mental pendulum toward OSAS, it swings far
enough to be devoid of NOSAS, so that most people in such circumstances,
at one time or another, believe in a purely free OSAS.25

Legalism is not Saving
       Since those who reject OSAS are conditioning their salvation on their
performance, standard arguments against the performance-based mentality
apply to the first two points.

       Works
                    Whereas strict legalists trust in their good works for
                    eternal life, the Bible counters that salvation from hell “is
                    by grace, it is no longer on the basis of works, otherwise
                    grace is no longer grace” (Rom 11:6). If we could get to
                    heaven by being good, then Christ did not have to die.
                   Thus, those who trust in their own goodness for eternal life
are saying in effect that Christ’s death was unnecessary. Clearly, such
legalists have failed to trust in Christ for eternal life.
Appendix 2. Oscillation is not Salvation                               Page 107

       Faith and Works
                    Soft legalists trust in their good works and in Christ for
                    the gift of eternal life. But in doing so they are saying, in
                    effect, that Christ’s death was not good enough, it was
                    insufficient. Thus, they insult Christ rather than trust
                    Christ. For this reason, the Bible warns that we are
                    “justified by faith apart from works” (Rom 3:28). “But to
the one who does not work, but believes in Him who justifies the ungodly,
his faith is counted as righteousness” (Rom 4:5). We must trust in Christ
rather than trust in what we do for Christ.
     Proveitists add works as a condition for entering heaven. They teach a
false gospel that ultimately conditions entrance into heaven on a faith that
works (= faith + works). Such teachers are really wolves in sheep’s clothing
(Mt 7:15) who deny salvation by faith alone. They appeal to their good
works as necessary proof of salvation. From their perspective, good works
(in terms of one’s moral God-enabled performance) are necessary to enter
heaven. In the end, proveitists are performatists.26

       Faith Alone
                We cannot be saved by believing in both Jesus and our good
                works for the gift of eternal life. Jesus paid the full purchase
                price with His precious blood (1Pet 1:18-19), not merely the
                down payment. We must receive salvation as a free gift
                without trying to earn it. “For by grace you have been saved
                through faith; and that not of yourselves, it is the gift of
God; not as a result of works, that no one should boast” (Eph 2:8-9). “The
free gift of God is eternal life in Christ” (Rom 6:23). We are “justified as a
gift by His grace” (Rom 3:24). We must believe that what Jesus has done is
sufficient and that the only condition we must meet for that salvation is faith
alone.

Oscillation is not Necessarily Saving
        As to the third OSAS-U option, one could only wish that it were
reasonably true that on the forward swing of the pendulum many, if not
most, legalists temporarily abandon their legalism. The OSAS-N argument
adopted herein, however, is that confusion between receiving eternal life as a
gift and earning it as a reward, more often than not, leads to damnation.
        People who think that they are receiving eternal life as a gift while
(logically) trying to earn it as a reward do not get it as a gift—ever. As long
as they have the notion in the back of their mind that their possession of the
gift of eternal life necessarily involves their performance (as a requirement
from God), they are prevented from coming to saving faith.
Page 108                                   Woolly Wolves and Woolless Sheep
        To express this matter in terms of percentages, if a person is 99%
persuaded that eternal life is a gift, yet 1% persuaded that good performance
is also necessary in order to have this gift, then such an individual does not
genuinely believe that the gift of eternal life is truly a free gift.
        While the momentum of the sermon temporarily might stress the
freeness of the gospel, a subconscious gravitation in the back of the
congregates’ minds (tugging on their consciousness)—developed by the
emphasis they have heard in many other sermons and invitations—pulls
them simultaneously into believing that this free gift really costs them
something (really everything to some degree). They never really believe,
100%, that the free gift is truly free.27 To really believe that the offer is
genuinely free, they would have to completely break this backward pull into
legalism. Thus, they do not come to saving faith. In short, the faith shown in
Illustration 53 does not save.
                       Illustration 54. Forward Swing




      Misconstruing the free and costly aspects of eternal life can be
compared to a rocking horse. On the forward rock (or swing to speak in
pendulum terms), a person is told that the eternal life that gets them into
heaven is a free gift.
                      Illustration 55. Backward Swing
Appendix 2. Oscillation is not Salvation                                  Page 109

        On the backward rock (or swing), the congregants are informed of the
personal cost involved. The congregants sitting in the pews (and prospects
outside the church, who are given evangelistic tracts) are invited to take the
water of life freely by making Christ Lord of their lives. Implicitly at the
very least (and sometimes explicitly), making Christ Lord of their lives is
linked with making Christ Lord of the way they live. Making Him Lord of
the way they live is, in turn, tied inseparably with making Him Lord of their
performance. The bottom line is that receiving the free gift is conditioned on
their performance. The reputedly free gift is certainly not free!
        Securitists realize that such evangelistic presentations of the gospel
obscure the saving message of the gospel. In fact, such presentations are
deadly distortions. You cannot be saved by believing (even partially) in your
performance. Nevertheless, many securitists hope that (at the apex of the
forward swing toward believing in the freeness of the gift) most legalists
come to saving faith.
        Psychologically, such an assumption is questionable. Biblically, this
wishful thinking is unacceptable. The narrow gate is much too narrow to
allow that most of those within professing Christendom will enter heaven.
Either the majority of professing believers are excluded because of their
defective performance (so performatists), or the majority of those professing
faith in Christ are excluded because of their defective faith (so OSAS-N
securitists).*
        If the prevalent opinion is granted that the narrow gate is dealing with
entrance into heaven (Mt 7:15), then OSAS-U securitists are left without a
leg on which to stand. For in that case, why are the majority of professing
Christians lost? OSAS-U can appeal neither to performance nor to defective
faith (in the majority of the cases) to explain why the majority are rejected.
        Similar problems arise from other passages, such as the wheat and the
tares (Mt 13:24-30,36-43). If the vast majority of those who believe the
costly-free perversion are saved, then the devil would have a devil of a time
sowing any tares and keeping them tares until harvest! Practically all the
tares the devil sowed would turn into wheat. If OSAS-U were true, then
practically all tares would turn into wheat, if not immediately then at least at
a moment of oscillation. The Lord’s angels would have no need to be
concerned about the tares since the tares would turn into wheat anyway. As
it is, angels are very concerned and rightly so. Thus, the lack of concern on
the part of OSAS-U is completely unjustified.
        Sandwiched in-between Jesus’ presentation and discussion of the
wheat and the tares, He introduces the parable of the mustard seed and also
the parable of the leaven. As to the mustard seed, this mustard plant mutates
into a grotesque tree. The monstrous growth of the mustard seed results in a

*
    See Illustration 50. Three Contending Views of the Narrow Gate, 99.
Page 110                                     Woolly Wolves and Woolless Sheep
plant so large that even the birds of the air (i.e., false converts) find rest in
it—that is, in the malignant Church (Mt 13:31-33). Advocates of OSAS-U
have confused the Church Triumphant with the Church Malignant. Leaven,
birds, and tares do not genuine converts make.
        By and large, as pictured by Scripture, the devil is successful at
sowing (and keeping) tares among the wheat, saturating the dough with
leaven, and making room for his birds among genuine believers. Surely, at
times, rare as they may be percentagewise, some of the devil’s masquerading
believers actually come to saving faith. Even so, the time of their coming to
saving faith cannot be at the same time that they believe the false gospel
used by Satan to infiltrate the Christian ranks. The legalistic gospel used by
Satan to infiltrate does not regenerate.
                 Illustration 56. Breaking the Rocking Horse




       Something in the thinking of Satan’s infiltrators must snap, at least
long enough for them to snap out of Satan’s legalistic snare, so that they
come to a realization that the free gift is truly free—100%. The rocking
horse must break. If the rocking horse never breaks, then those duped by
Satan into believing the false legalistic gospel are never saved.
       At some point, and a 99% oscillation does not qualify as that point,
those listening to the costly-free perversion of the gospel must recognize
(through the convicting power of the Holy Spirit) that the free aspect of
eternal life that has been granted them (as a consequence of their simply
trusting in Christ for the eternal life as a free gift) unconditionally assures
them of reaching heaven. In order to be saved independently of their
performance, they must at some point come to conclude that they are saved
from hell independent of their performance, despite their being told
repeatedly by pastors and evangelists that their good performance is
necessary for salvation from hell.
       As long as these would-be converts ascribe any saving necessity to
their performance, they cannot be saved independently of their performance.
It does not matter if they verbally acknowledge that their performance is
Appendix 2. Oscillation is not Salvation                                 Page 111

meritorious. As a rule, they will not. Instead, they will deceive themselves
into thinking that it is okay to rely on their mythical nonmeritorious
performance for salvation from eternal damnation.

Software Examples
       As to the OSAS-U rejection of the soteriological necessity of security
because of the alleged lack of biblical perspicuity, is it really that difficult to
distinguish a free gift from a costly reward even if eternal life is referred to
in both capacities?
       That a singular benefit (namely eternal life) may be both free and
costly without all aspects of that benefit (such as entrance into heaven) being
costly is not that difficult of a concept to grasp. Surely, in this day and age,
we realize that a benefit can be both free and costly without freely entitling
one to all the aspects of that benefit. Conversely, a benefit can be both free
and costly without making all aspects of that benefit costly. In the software
industry, for example, one can get various types of free software.

•     freeware (programs that are completely free),
•     adware (programs sponsored by annoying ads),
•     nagware (programs that are free but nag you to buy them),
•     timeware (programs that are free for a limited period of time),
•     guiltware (programs that are free but plead for you to make a
      contribution to the programmer),*
•     careware (programs that are free but prompt you to make donations to
      the sponsored charity), †
•     crippleware (programs with free basic functions but costly advanced
      functions).

       Perhaps some sitting in a costly-free congregation might, in a moment
of oscillation, attempt to reconcile the pastoral contraction being presented
to them by regarding eternal life as genuinely free like adware. With such a
mindset, they might regard it as free and conclude that they just have to put
up with the prompts from the pastor to do other things now that they have
received the free benefit. In this way, maybe some congregants are able to
reconcile, in their minds at least, the fact that their pastor is claiming that the
eternal life that gets them into heaven is a free gift that costs them
everything. While this solution is hardly satisfactory, perchance some of
those sitting under such teaching might come to saving faith by means of
this misperception.

*
    Also called donationware.
†
    Also called donationware.
Page 112                                     Woolly Wolves and Woolless Sheep
        Or maybe people sitting in the pews of such churches might regard
the purportedly costly-free gift as nagware. They can have it for free if they
are just willing to put up with a nagging pastor who is going to pester them
to do more than receive eternal life as a free gift. Again, such a perspective
is far from ideal. Nevertheless, one might concede to the OSAS-U
perspective that in such a case, misguided individuals might conceivably
come to saving faith through the drawing of the Holy Spirit.
        Timeware is really out of the question though, contrary to OSAS-U.
Believing in Christ for temporary life is not the same thing as believing in
Christ for eternal life. Those who believe that eternal life is only free
temporarily do not believe in Christ savingly. They believe that their
possession of eternal life is conditioned on their performance. From their
perspective, if their performance (i.e., their perseverance) were to dip below
some nebulous threshold, they would lose the gift of life that is necessary to
get them into heaven. Unfortunately for the OSAS-U point of view, most
costly-free perspectives are laced with this poisoned perspective, if not
composed entirely of this conviction. But even one drop of this persuasion is
enough to nullify the possibly of saving faith. A faith composed of even 1%
of this poison is still far too deadly to be saving.
        A guiltware perspective, on the other hand, might qualify for saving
faith. In this understanding of the gospel, God gives us eternal life freely, but
we should feel guilty if we do not do anything for God in return. After all,
we should not bite the hand that feeds us, so to speak. We should love Jesus
because He has first loved us, has died for us, and has given eternal life to us
as a free gift. This presentation has a ring of biblical truth to it. Stated as
such, one could easily believe that eternal life is genuinely free—if it were
not for the fact that performatists constantly offset this perspective with the
additive that if you do not respond in the prescribed manner, then you are
not saved. Moral obligations are made soteric necessities by performatists.
        In other words, this guiltware presentation correctly teaches that
eternal life is a free gift and that we should respond morally with
thanksgiving expressed in holy lives for having been given such a gift. The
problem is that performatists do not leave the matter there but follow up by
conditioning the possession of the gift on the moral performance that should
logically follow. Performatists change should into must. Not only should you
live a holy life in gratitude for the gift that God has given you, you must do
so or forfeit the gift. The average congregant will fail to perceive the fatal
poison in such a legalistic cup. Therefore, although a person could be saved
by adopting a guiltware perspective, it is highly doubtful that many of them
will respond savingly by adopting this perspective because this perspective
will be spiked with deadly toxins that mutate it into something else other
than sheer gratitude. Should will have become must in the back of their
minds, preventing them from drinking freely from the water of life.
Appendix 2. Oscillation is not Salvation                               Page 113

        Likewise, someone adopting a careware outlook conceivably might
come to think that eternal life really is a free gift. According to this mindset,
you should help others because God has done so much for you in freely
saving you. We should lovingly serve others because God lovingly saved
us—freely. To be sure, considerable truth is found in this perspective. Yet,
once again, the problem remains that the congregant may well adopt such an
attitude but simultaneously add a legalistic spin to it: If you do not help
others, then you are not saved and will not go to heaven. Helping others is
made necessary to help oneself to heaven. As above, should is mutated into
must. Thus, logically, the gift cannot be free.
        So while the guiltware and careware vantage points have the
advantage of underlying biblical truth, they easily are counterbalanced by
the offsetting legalistic notion that a morally responsible response is really a
soteriologically necessary response. The contributions and donations that
morally should be given in response to receiving the free gift are not
genuinely optional in proveitism. Payment is mandatory. Thus, in
performatistic theology, the freeware aspect of such approaches truly is
missing.
        The best approach is to break the back of the legalistic argument by
pointing out that the free and costly aspects of eternal life deal with two
different dimensions of the same concept. In terms of software, crippleware
is the backbreaker of legalism. The basic function of eternal life (namely
regeneration resulting in one’s name being permanently inscribed in the
Book of Life and unconditionally guaranteeing entrance into heaven) is
entirely free. One needs only to believe—once—in Christ for the free gift of
eternal life in order to have it permanently. Once saved always saved, in
terms of heaven versus hell, is the unconditional result. This dimension of
eternal life is fully, freely, and unconditionally guaranteed from the initial
point of reception forward—forever.
        Naturally, as most using crippleware already suspect anyway, strings
are attached. But those strings do not pertain to the free aspect. The gift is
free. Those functions of eternal life that are costly have nothing to do with
retaining regeneration, keeping one’s name in the Book of Life, or entering
heaven. Instead, rulership in the future societal regeneration, having one’s
name recorded in the Book for Life, and additional heavenly pleasures are at
stake on the costly side of the equation.
        The Bible already has set the stage for the crippleware analogy above.
Granted, the Bible does not use computer software to provide the
illustration; nevertheless, even more concrete imagery is employed by the
biblical text. According to the Bible, the water of life (outside the city at
least) is free—absolutely free! Access to the tree of life (inside the city) and
wearing the crown of life, in sharp contrast, are very costly. By making such
strong delineations, the Bible has broken the back of proveitism’s legalistic
rocking horse. The water is free; the tree and crown are costly.
Page 114                                     Woolly Wolves and Woolless Sheep

Subconscious
        Such biblical emphases logically break the back of the legalistic
argument, but Satan’s minions are not going to back down without a fight.
Unless something eradicates the legalism planted in the back of the minds of
most congregants long enough to throw their legalism into sufficient
remission (so that it does not prevent them from coming to the saving
realization that their performance truly is not a requirement for the free gift),
those sitting in the typical proveitist or forfeitist congregations never will
come to saving faith, not even for one second. They may say that the gift is
free, but in terms of logical consistency, they do not genuinely believe that it
actually is free because they believe that their possession of eternal life
hinges on their performance via repentance and perseverance.
        Performatists are fond of saying that Christ is either Lord of all or not
Lord at all. If that were the case, then Peter could not have responded to the
Lord by saying, “By no means, Lord” (Acts 10:14; 11:8). If genuine
believers can say, No Lord, then obviously subjective Lordship is not all or
nothing. Lordship pertaining to one’s performance is not an all-or-nothing
affair. In contrast, whether one actually excludes one’s performance from
saving faith is, from the biblical perspective, an all-or-nothing matter.
Poisoning saving faith with one drop of one’s performance is wholly deadly.
                    Illustration 57. Fatally Mistaken Faith




       The biblical solution is misapplied by legalistic practitioners so as to
make the solution part of the problem. The biblical demands regarding the
costly aspects of eternal life are superimposed by legalists upon the simple
requirement that the free aspects of eternal life be taken freely. Mass
confusion is the result. The biblical injunction to believe in Jesus is twisted
into a necessity of serving Jesus—for the free gift!28 Such birdbrained
approaches are welcomed in the Church Malignant. Soteriological birds are
embraced in branches of professing Christendom. But perching in the church
does not make one a Christian anymore than standing in a carport makes one
a car. What was supposed to be a flock of sheep will (in the end) prove to be,
Appendix 2. Oscillation is not Salvation                              Page 115

for the most part, a flock of birds. The majority of the visible church
doctrinally has gone to the birds—just as Jesus foretold.
       From a Free Grace perspective, acknowledging that the majority of
professing Christians is lost would be impossible if NOSAS-U were true. In
contradistinction, NOSAS logically is able (given its conditional theological
framework) to attribute the lack of regeneration among the majority of
professing Christians to the substandard practice of such Christians. Free
Grace theology, however, is not at liberty to base regeneration on relentless
activity. If OSAS is true, then so is OSAS-N, necessarily.

Moral Transformation is not Regeneration
       Returning to the aforementioned example of good Joe* who thought
he was saved because (1) he believed in Christ and (2) experienced a moral
transformation, this would qualify for saving faith according to OSAS-U.†
Of course, I find this OSAS-U position quite hammy.‡
                  Illustration 58. Highly Questionable Faith




       My OSAS-N rejoinder to people like Joe is, “I believe in Christ, so I
am saved because I’ve undergone regeneration. I do not base my salvation
from hell on my performance.” Too much is at stake. While the neophyte
might think that Joe’s perspective provides additional security, actually quite
the opposite is true. Joe’s position is susceptible to deadly demonic
deception. Jesus relates an interesting parallel regarding moral
transformation:
      43
         Now when the unclean spirit goes out of a man, it passes
      through waterless places, seeking rest, and does not find it.

*
  See Bible Study, 90.
†
  See again Illustration 50. Three Contending Views of the Narrow Gate, 99.
‡
  See ham sandwich illustration in Bible Study, 90.
Page 116                                    Woolly Wolves and Woolless Sheep
      44
         Then it says, “I will return to my house from which I came”;
      and when it comes, it finds it unoccupied, swept, and put in
      order. 45 Then it goes, and takes along with it seven other spirits
      more wicked than itself, and they go in and live there; and the
      last state of that man becomes worse than the first. That is the
      way it will also be with this evil generation. (Mt 12:43-45)

       Jesus compares what may happen at the time of an individual’s moral
transformation to what was happening at the national level. Jesus and John
the Baptist had preached a message of repentance from sin and of faith in
Jesus as the promised Messiah. Furthermore, Jesus and His disciples had
cast out many demons from individuals throughout the nation of Israel.
       Much excitement was in the air. Lives were being changed. People
were repenting and being baptized. Demons were being cast out left and
right. Yet not all those who experienced moral transformation because of
their moral repentance or demonic deliverance experienced regeneration.
Not all those with a wonderful testimony of radical moral transformation
(even because of Jesus) necessarily had experienced regeneration. Not all
those who had experienced moral or demonic deliverance had gone on to
experience saving faith. Nationally, many had repented, but not all those
who repented of their sins went on to believe in Jesus for eternal life.
       From a legalistic perspective, why should they? They now had a
wonderful testimony of a radical moral change in which they could trust for
eternal life. They had believed in Christ for moral transformation. Now they
could know that they were saved. Right? Wrong. Moral transformation does
not prove regeneration. Undoubtedly, Jesus’ name may be credited to a
considerable degree with having effected their moral transformation, but He
had not necessarily granted them regeneration. Similarly, in Mt 7:22 many
lost preachers will think that they were saved because they will have
produced radical moral transformations in the lives of others (such as their
converts), even by casting out demons in Jesus’ name. Still, Jesus is not
impressed. Their last state is worse than their first.
       Before their radical transformation and demonic deliverance, such
people knew they needed help. They were more easily convicted of their
wretched state. Many of them knew they were lost. Now that they have
experienced a moral transformation, some of them are seven times harder to
lead to faith in Christ for eternal life. The demonic deception would be seven
times harder to break now that they have become legalists with wonderful
testimonies of God’s transforming grace.
       Without a doubt they had experienced a wonderful transformation
because of God’s grace. Unfortunately, they mistook transforming grace for
saving grace. Now that they have become good Joes by the power of God’s
grace, they cannot believe that they lack eternal life. However, one cannot
get to heaven by trusting in Christ for a moral transformation any more than
Appendix 2. Oscillation is not Salvation                            Page 117

one can get to heaven by trusting in Christ for a fish sandwich (cp. Jn 6:1-
64).

Symmetry
       A good Joe frequently will fail to perceive that he is conditioning his
salvation on his behavior. After all, he asserts, “I am saved because I
believe.” Yet in the back of his mind, he simultaneously is thinking, “I am
saved because I behave (as a result of having believed).” From his
perspective, both statements are true but not contradictory because the
behavior is self-perceived as mere evidence of salvation.
                    Illustration 59. Free Grace Statements




        Contrasting good Joe’s perspective with a Free Grace perspective
may be helpful to show the difference. Like good Joe, I can assert, “I am
saved because I believe.” Unlike good Joe, in the back of my mind, I simply
am thinking, “I am saved because I have eternal life (as a result of having
believed).” No works-righteousness is planted in the back of my mind. The
same reason I am saved from hell is the very reason I will be saved from
hell—because I have the free gift of eternal life. Soteriologically, both my
initial salvation and my final salvation exclude my behavior as a factor.
                     Illustration 60. Free Grace Symmetry




The same reason I was saved initially is the very reason I can turn around
and say that I will be saved finally—because I have eternal life. Behavior is
not a factor: Believe ⇒ saved/have eternal life ⇒ will be saved.
Page 118                                    Woolly Wolves and Woolless Sheep
                     Illustration 61. Proveitist Statements




       A good Joe, on the other hand, is banking on his good behavior. To
be sure, the sequence he perceives is: believe ⇒ saved ⇒ good behavior. He
assumes that he has made behavior the result rather than the savior so that he
will be saved because he has been saved—as proven by his good behavior.
                     Illustration 62. Proveitist Symmetry




        In actuality, however, he also affirms that he will be saved because of
this intermediate behavior: Believe ⇒ saved ⇒ behave ⇒ saved. His future
salvation is conditioned not only on his initial belief but on his subsequent
behavior: Believe ⇒ has been saved ⇒ behave ⇒ will be saved.

Birth Certificate
        A proveitist preacher at the church that my family and I attend
rebuked those who trust in the biblical promises of eternal life as their basis
for assurance. To illustrate his point, he said that the way you know that you
are alive is if you are moving and breathing, not by looking at your birth
certificate: Present performance rather than biblical promises prove life.
        Aside from conditioning heaven on performance, his argument
necessitates logically that sheep are the only ones performing spiritual
activity. Supposedly, sheep are discerned as having eternal life because of
their good lives. Sheep live good lives. Goats live bad lives. So sheep go to
heaven, and goats to hell. Again, aside from teaching a false gospel based on
performance as necessary evidence, this position demonstrates fuzzy
thinking. Sheep are not the only ones demonstrating signs of life. Goats go
to church. Goats help people. Goats breathe and move. So a goat cannot be
discerned from sheep by this type of performance. Some goats outside the
church are better morally than some sheep inside the church. Thus, a sheep
cannot be discerned from a goat by spiritual performance.
Appendix 2. Oscillation is not Salvation                               Page 119

       This proveitist preacher thought that he was going to heaven because
he lives better than the goats. I tend to think that such preachers are goats.
For they base their salvation on their moral performance. “What then? Are
we [sheep] better than they [i.e., better than legalistic goats]? Not at all; for
we have already charged that…‘There is none righteous, not even one’”
(Rom 3:9-10). No one is going to get to heaven by being better than others.
Moreover, the Bible says that some sheep are worse than goats (1Tim 5:8).
Going to heaven is a matter of being a believer, not a matter of being better.

Reverse Mentality
       Surely, in trying to relegate works merely to providing proof of
salvation, some proveitists would at least suggest a reverse articulation.
Rather than admit they believe that they are going to heaven because they
live better than the goats, they would say that because they live better than
the goats, they are going to heaven. Allegedly, living better is just the proof
that they are saved, not the condition for being saved.
                     Illustration 63. Legalistic Repentance




       This reverse articulation is suggested by the fact that this particular
proveitist preacher within our church stated that in order to go to heaven,
one must repent. Conversely, he also stipulated that if one repents in order to
go to heaven, one will go to hell. He considered the latter articulation to be
an example of legalistic repentance. Indeed, it is. However, what he failed to
note is that his alternative articulation, likewise, was legalistic in that it
conditions entrance into heaven on one’s performance. By making such
proof necessary, proveitists cannot avoid making it a condition.
Page 120                                     Woolly Wolves and Woolless Sheep
                Illustration 64. Legalistic Filling in the Blank




       Proveitistic breathing is not just proof that you are alive; it is
necessary to stay alive soteriologically and to reach heaven eschatologically.
This breathing represents many things in proveitist theology: Repent or die.
Produce good works or go to hell. Persevere or perish. Bear or burn. Thus,
the legalistic blank might be filled in by many things within proveitistic
theology: repent, produce, persevere, bear, or run (to name but a few).
•   In order to reach heaven you must repent. But if you repent in order to
    reach heaven you will go to hell.
•   In order to reach heaven you must produce good fruits. But if you
    produce good works in order to reach heaven you will go to hell.
•   In order to reach heaven you must persevere. But if you persevere in
    order to reach heaven you will go to hell.
•   In order to reach heaven you must bear good fruits. But if you bear good
    fruits in order to reach heaven you will go to hell.
•   In order to reach heaven you must run. But if you run in order to reach
    heaven you will go to hell.

        Many proveitists think that the prize Paul was running to win in
1Cor 9:24-27 was entrance into heaven. Seriously now, how can anyone
read that passage and entertain proveitistic reverse mentality? Paul certainly
is not saying, “In order to win, you must run. But if you run in order to win,
you will lose.” Logically, proveitism is laughable, not laudable.
Soteriologically, it is damnable.

     1
        A text such as 1Jn 3:10 is thought, by proveitists, to supply their
